71	- **Answer: No formal system**
72	- Engineers pushed back: "I cannot go and create a ticket every single time"
73	- Process is very informal - just ping and ask

85	- Options: Cisco laptop OR Cisco image on personal laptop
86	- Colin's laptop provisioning already initiated by Rahul

181	### 6. Srinivas's Technical Philosophy
182	
183	**Key Principles (Direct Quotes):**
184	
185	1. **Extensibility First:**
186	> "Always put two hats when you evaluate. One, will you solve my current need? Two, can it be extensible? Or can I today write the infrastructure in a way that it is available for agentic infrastructure?"
187	
188	2. **Agentic Infrastructure:**
189	> "Anything we do should be future proof and ready to enable the agentic infrastructure. So while you are solving your current need, we may be solving another agentic infrastructure behind the scenes."
190	
191	3. **Reusability:**
192	> "You need to step back and say, how do I make this infrastructure generally so that we can leverage it in other places. So you guys are not building a pointed solution, but you're building infrastructure pieces where I can leverage in other places."
193	
194	4. **Direct Communication:**
195	> "Once you start working, it's engineer-to-engineer conversation. You'll find a good partner."
196	
197	5. **Open Disagreement:**
198	> "You can always correct me saying that you are wrong. I don't mind in the private or for me it doesn't matter. From the technical point of view, it doesn't matter if you can catch me anywhere, even in peak meetings."
199	
200	6. **Fast Pace:**
201	> "I go very fast, very, very fast. People know me who are working with me. And sometimes, team might say, why is Srini so aggressive, right? Because that's my nature."
202	
203	7. **Colleague Relationship:**
204	> "Once you are onboarding, you are my friend. So I'll treat you the way or treat me the same way as a colleague."

403	## Key Insights
404	
405	1. **Dramatically reduced AI scope:** DeepSight platform means BayOne doesn't need to build AI infrastructure from scratch. This changes the entire engagement model - focus shifts to application logic, prompts, and integration rather than infrastructure.
406	
407	2. **Existing CI/CD app exists:** There's already a CI/CD application (Rui's work) launching in 2-3 weeks. BayOne extends this rather than starting fresh. Need to coordinate handoff with Rui.
408	
409	3. **Cultural fit confirmed:** Srinivas explicitly values direct communication, disagreement, and engineering-first thinking. Colin's "10-year test" philosophy resonated. This is a collaborative technical partnership, not a vendor relationship.
410	
411	4. **Bazel context critical:** The team is stressed from Bazel production rollout. This explains limited availability and sets expectation that Cisco engineers are under pressure.
412	
413	5. **Infrastructure bottleneck known:** ADS machine provisioning is a known pain point for all new engineers. Anand agreed to monitor this engagement as a test case for improving the process.
414	
415	6. **Informal culture - risk and benefit:** No ticketing, no formal processes means fast iteration but no paper trail. Need to use WebEx space effectively and request recordings.
416	
417	7. **MCP mentioned by Colin:** Colin proactively mentioned wanting to build "some kind of MCP" for Jenkins/GitHub integration - aligns with modern tooling patterns.
418

## User

Tool Result: 1	# Meeting 2: Regression Testing & UI Automation with Rama
2	
3	**Date:** February 17, 2026
4	**Location:** Cisco Office, 3rd Floor (in-person, Room 73)
5	**Duration:** ~20-25 minutes
6	**Recording Status:** Not recorded
7	
8	---
9	
10	## Participants
11	
12	| Name | Organization | Role | Scope in Meeting |
13	|------|--------------|------|------------------|
14	| Colin Moore | BayOne | Director of AI | Technical discussion, solution ideation |
15	| Rama (Ramagar) | Cisco | Test Manager, Nexus Dashboard | Problem statement presenter, domain expert |
16	| Rahul Bobbili | BayOne | Delivery | Facilitator, introductions |
17	
18	**Context:** Rahul connected Colin with Rama opportunistically during the on-site visit. This is a separate project from the CI/CD work with Arun's team, but has significant technical crossover.
19	
20	---
21	
22	## Meeting Context
23	
24	**How This Meeting Happened:**
25	Rahul was walking Colin around and saw an opportunity to connect him with Rama ("If you're available, we'll get you connected to our AI person"). Informal, opportunistic introduction.
26	
27	**Rama's Domain:**
28	- **Team:** Nexus Dashboard testing (network controllers)
29	- **Scope:** UI and API testing for SDN (Software-Defined Networking) controllers
30	- **Products:** Visualization, provisioning, and intent-driven network management
31	- **Scale:** 30,000-60,000 test cases running daily across multiple groups
32	
33	**Relationship to CI/CD Project:**
34	- **Arun's team** (CI/CD project): Tests switch/router functionality directly (CLI, functional conformance)
35	- **Rama's team** (this meeting): Tests Nexus Dashboard (controller that SENDS commands to switches)
36	- They're complementary: "My job will be done, that's it. As long as I kick in that CLI, I don't care whether [Arun's team] is doing the same job or not."
37	
38	---
39	
40	## Problem Statements (From Rama)
41	
42	### Problem 1: Regression Analysis (Primary Pain Point)
43	
44	**The Scale:**
45	- 30,000-60,000 test cases run daily
46	- Jenkins automatically queues jobs
47	- Runs complete in ~12 hours
48	- Results need manual analysis
49	
50	**The Pain:**
51	- 10-12 engineers spend 3-4+ hours daily analyzing results
52	- Each engineer reviews 5-6 test suites
53	- Early in release cycle: many failures, chaos ("it's a nightmare")
54	- Late in release cycle: fewer failures, more stable
55	- Engineers questioned: "Did you really analyze everything?"
56	
57	**The Ask:**
58	> "How do we provide these AI tools can do this kind of failure analysis?"
59	
60	**Example Given:**
61	UI timeout errors cascade across 60 test suites, affecting 2000+ test cases. Engineers manually trace back to root cause. AI could identify: "This one bug is impacting these many test cases" instantly.
62	
63	**Key Quote (Rama):**
64	> "Regression analysis is one of the costly functions. Where our op-ex is being a little bit overspent, we want to manage it better or use that bandwidth to develop automation or do something else."
65	
66	### Problem 2: UI Automation (Secondary Pain Point)
67	
68	**Context:**
69	- Currently heavy on API-based testing
70	- Leadership (Milesh, Nilesha, Sonawee) pushing to "move the needle" on UI automation
71	- UI testing is "laborious work"
72	
73	**Current Stack:**
74	- Selenium tools
75	- Cisco automation infrastructure layer for Python
76	- Shared Git repository (cross-Cisco reusable)
77	
78	**The Pain:**
79	- UI changes require massive script updates
80	- Example: Simple UI change required modifying 4,000 scripts
81	
82	**Key Quote (Rama):**
83	> "UAE [UI Automation] is not impossible, but it is a more laborious work."
84	
85	### Problem 3: UI Theme Changes (Emerging Pain Point)
86	
87	**Context:**
88	- Cisco moving to dark theme / night mode
89	- Previously white background, now black
90	- Different color schemas for different themes
91	
92	**The Challenge:**
93	- Traffic thresholds shown as green/yellow/red
94	- Does same schema apply to dark theme?
95	- Need to re-validate all screenshots/visual comparisons
96	- Some places modified, some not - need to catch inconsistencies
97	
98	**Key Quote (Rama):**
99	> "Last time you showed us... dark blue and then it was night, black color. So then what happens is three shots [screenshots]. Some screenshots will be there..."
100	
101	---
102	
103	## Colin's Technical Response
104	
105	### On Test Selection (SRT)
106	Colin probed whether test selection was a pain point. Rama clarified:
107	- **Selective Regression Testing (SRT)** already exists
108	- Based on code changes, chooses relevant 1,000-1,500 tests vs. all 40,000
109	- Enterprise and AS/NK teams use this
110	- Not the current bottleneck
111	
112	### On Failure Analysis Hierarchy
113	Colin described the dual relationship between test failures:
114	
115	**Hierarchical:**
116	> "Sometimes it's a repeat error that's flagged, but it was already covered by this up here. It's kind of just noise at that point. If you fix this one, it fixes the downstream."
117	
118	**Dependency-based:**
119	> "Other times... this is happening because this one, so there's a dependency more than there's a hierarchy."
120	
121	**Rama's Response:**
122	> "I think that is the complex one... how you correlate, there is [a situation where] you are using three different products... and one entity's [failure] symptom is being reflected on the UI."
123	
124	### On Graph Topology Solution
125	Colin proposed a solution from the CI/CD work:
126	
127	**The Approach:**
128	- Build a graph topology of the codebase
129	- Multi-dimensional representation of relationships
130	- Files, libraries, dependencies all mapped
131	- **State-aware:** Graph updates as code changes
132	- **Efficient:** No live queries needed; pre-computed relationships
133	
134	**Use Cases:**
135	1. **Impact Analysis:** "If I want to see what files a library touches... how do I know what impact [a change] will have?"
136	2. **Test Activation:** "Because this changed, here are the ones that are relevant that should be activated"
137	3. **Failure Hierarchy:** "If it's a test that fails, now I know the hierarchy, which one is essentially the primary affected party"
138	4. **UI Change Impact:** Rama asked - "How much effort for reflecting [UI changes] in your scripts?" The graph could answer automatically.
139	
140	**Rama's Response:**
141	> "I got what you mentioned. But yeah, I think that's a good part to fix this."
142	
143	**Caveat Acknowledged:**
144	> "But it requires, yes, the executable commit may be, guys, you need to make structural changes on your core test, all these things, how you build the database kind of thing now."
145	
146	### On UI Automation Demo

12	### Q1: Is there an internal ticketing system (ServiceNow, Jira, etc.) we should use to request access?
13	
14	**Answer:** No formal ticketing system in use. The team tried Jira for about a year but received significant pushback from engineers who said they couldn't create a ticket every time they needed something. The culture is very informal - people ping directly and say "take care of this." Divakar noted: "We are used to very informal... today I don't think there is an informal to talk something."
15	
16	The preferred method is the WebEx space (BayOne CICD WG). Anand reinforced this, saying if questions aren't getting answered, escalate through the WebEx space and he'll help expedite. Srinivas also emphasized using the WebEx space and said he'd add engineers to the group who can answer questions.
17	
18	**Implication:** No ticket system to request access through. Use WebEx space for all requests. Anand and Srinivas will monitor and help unblock if needed.
19	
20	**Status:** ANSWERED
21	
22	---
23	
24	### Q2: Who is the single point of contact responsible for ensuring BayOne team members receive access?
25	
26	**Answer:** Divakar is the primary point of contact for access. When asked directly, he said: "At least for the ones which are on the top, I would be the one." He specifically mentioned he has full context on Jenkins and will handle provisioning ADS machines (Linux machines needed for code access and building).
27	
28	However, different teams own different systems, so Divakar will need to coordinate:
29	- **GitHub Enterprise:** Requires training (3-4 hours), then Divakar can grant access after completion
30	- **Jenkins:** Divakar has full context and direct ownership
31	- **Airflow:** Needs to contact another team
32	- **CAT:** Needs to contact another team
33	- **DevX:** Another team owns it, but "we can get to that data as well"
34

## Current Situation

**The engagement:** BayOne is building AI-powered CI/CD pipeline tooling for Cisco's Cloud Networking Group (Nexus 9000 switches). Six deliverables scoped (A through F), phased over a year at ~$100K/quarter.

**The crisis:** It's now **end of March 2026**. The SOW contract start date was November 2025, but:
- Cisco's procurement delayed signing by 6+ weeks
- Hardware provisioning took another month+
- The Feb 17 in-person discovery meetings happened, but actual development work has **not started**

That's ~5 months of calendar time burned with zero deliverables produced. Cisco is understandably frustrated despite the delays being largely on their side (procurement, hardware, access provisioning).

**What's been done:**
- Extensive internal planning (resource plans, role descriptions, JDs, cost estimates, quarterly phasing)
- Feb 17 in-person discovery at Cisco (met Anand, Divakar, Srinivas, Rama)
- Learned about DeepSight Atlas platform (changes the AI infrastructure approach significantly)
- Answered ~20 of 65 discovery questions
- Identified key contacts and access requirements

**What hasn't happened:**
- No team members fully onboarded with access
- No code written
- No deliverables produced
- Many discovery questions still unanswered

98	The program agreement executed between the supplier and Cisco governs this SOW (the "Program Agreement"). In the event of a conflict between this SOW and the Program Agreement, the provisions of the Program Agreement prevail.
99	
100	Once finalized, this SOW begins on the Start Date identified within the C-Worker connect associated "Project " and remains in effect until the later of: (i) completion and acceptance of all Milestones and other Deliverables; or (ii) the identified End Date, unless terminated earlier in accordance with the Program Agreement.
101	
102	By accepting this SOW, the supplier is agreeing to the terms of this SOW as governed by the Program Agreement.
103	
104	### 2 Services and Work Product
105	
106	#### 2.1 Services Objectives
107	
108	**Organization background:**
109	
110	This scope is being requested by Cisco's Cloud Networking Group (CN) Test team. This team is responsible for validating (regression and automation tests) the generic engineering releases and customer specials (specific customer requests) releases for Nexus 9000 (switches) product line along with the development of required infrastructure tools.
111	
112	Cisco NX-OS (Nexus operating system) Software is a data center-class operating system built with modularity, resiliency, and serviceability at its foundation. Cisco NX-OS helps ensure continuous availability for mission-critical data center environments and provides a robust feature set that fulfils the switching and storage networking needs of data centers.
113	
114	**Outsourced:**
115	
116	To determine the best user experience in upcoming NX-OS releases, Cisco needs to execute automation and regression testing of the features in an upcoming NX-OS release.
117	
118	**Impact/Benefit:**
119	
120	Apart from cost saving, the other benefits of this service is speed of delivery, quality and consistency with Cisco internal brand guidelines.
121	
122	**Supplier management of resource:**
123	
124	The supplier will manage the Service outcome along with the resources. The supplier will be responsible for managing the resources in regard to ensuring they understand and complete the project to satisfaction as well as provide any necessary training. The supplier is responsible for replacing the resource with minimal to no disruption to Cisco or the Service. Supplier is responsible for the service outcome. Supplier has a lead who is primary point of contact and all work is routed through the lead.
125

## User

Tool Result: 1	Meeting Summary (Clean & Accurate)
2	The team reviewed the six problem areas and aligned on which use cases to start with.
3	Based on scope, complexity, and immediate feasibility, the group agreed that:
4	•	A – Developer Box (DevBox visibility, insights, AI-assisted debugging)
5	•	F – Branch Health / CD Health (failure attribution, automation, dashboards)
6	…are the best starting points for the initial engagement.
7	Use Case E – Self-Healing is valuable but the most complex, and will be addressed later once there is deeper understanding of the environment.
8	Anand emphasized that this is not a traditional staff-augmentation project — success depends on:
9	•	The right mindset (startup-style, iterative, problem-solving)
10	•	A high-touch first few weeks
11	•	Strong collaboration with Cisco internal engineers who know the systems
12	•	No introduction of external “products” or tooling being pushed in — work must be built on Cisco’s existing stack.
13	To start effectively:
14	•	The team needs access, a clear technical walkthrough, and a Cisco engineer with some bandwidth to partner during discovery.
15	•	Colin and Sarang will be involved on the Cisco side, but bandwidth is limited, so identifying an additional internal engineer is important.
16	Budget was discussed at a high-level only:
17	•	A rough starting range of $150–$200K for the initial quarter
18	•	Anand will confirm what can realistically be approved.
19	The intent is:
20	1.	Start with a lightweight discovery phase (1–2 weeks)
21	2.	Get clarity on the technical environment
22	3.	Produce a scoped plan + estimates
23	4.	Begin with 1–1.5 FTE onshore initially, followed by 4–5 offshore resources as the work scales
24	________________________________________
25	Next Steps
26	For Cisco (Anand + Team)
27	•	Confirm budget availability for the initial quarter.
28	•	Identify the internal CI/CD engineer who can partner closely during discovery.
29	•	Provide access / walkthrough sessions for the DevBox and CD pipeline areas.
30	•	Align internally that A & F are the starting focus areas.
31	For BayOne
32	•	Prepare a short discovery plan outlining:
33	o	What will be covered in weeks 1–2
34	o	What access/resources are needed
35	o	Expected outputs (scope, estimates, approach)
36	•	Propose the initial team model (onshore + offshore split).
37	•	Begin lining up candidates with the required mindset (iterative, proactive, problem-solving).
38	Thanks,
39	Zahra

## User

Base directory for this skill: /home/cmoore/programming/ai_opportunities/.claude/skills/singularity

# Singularity

Consulting engagement orchestrator. Processes meeting transcripts, emails, call preps, and internal debriefs into blockchain-style research libraries. Produces client-facing deliverables and pricing models. Replaces and supersedes sales-forge.

## Hard Rules

1. **Blockchain style.** Research documents are numbered chronologically and NEVER edited after creation. New understanding goes in new documents that reference earlier ones.
2. **Multi-pass processing.** Transcripts are read multiple times, each pass focused on one topic. This is the single most important processing rule. It exists for context clearing, exhaustive capture, better organization, and natural parallelization. Write after every read, not once at the end.
3. **Ask, do not assume.** Always propose file lists and get user approval before writing research docs or spawning agents. The user controls what gets created. Different meetings warrant different breakdowns.
4. **Agents write their own files.** Deep-dive and research agents write directly to the engagement folder. Use `mode: "bypassPermissions"`. Never fall back to writing in the main session if an agent fails. Report the failure and ask how to proceed.
5. **Max 5 questions per batch.** Never overwhelm the user. Ask follow-up questions in subsequent rounds. Prioritize questions that gate decisions or unblock progress.
6. **Deliverables flow from research.** Client-facing documents are drafted from the research library, not from raw transcripts. The research library is the single source of truth.
7. **Everything is dated.** Every file in the engagement gets a date in its filename (YYYY-MM-DD). No exceptions. Date reflects the source material date, not the analysis date.
8. **No em dashes in deliverables.** Use commas, periods, or "and" instead. No individual names, no direct quotes, no contrastive framing ("It's not just X, it's Y"), no emojis, no contractions.
9. **Solution, never product.** BayOne builds custom, tailor-made solutions using proven methodology. Never position as an off-the-shelf product.
10. **Self-contained skill.** All reference files, templates, and assets live within `.claude/skills/singularity/`. No external dependencies except `.claude/context/` for shared company info.

---

## Document Header Format

**Every research document must start with this header.** Agents must include it in all files they write.

```markdown
# <Set Number> - <Source Type>: <Topic>

**Source:** /<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/source/<filename>
**Source Date:** <date> (<context description>)
**Document Set:** <set number> (<description of what this set covers>)
**Pass:** <what this specific read was focused on>

---
```

Example:
```markdown
# 02 - Meeting: Technical Use Cases (Deep Dive)

**Source:** /lam_research/ip_protection/source/lam_meeting_3122026.txt
**Source Date:** 2026-03-12 (Discovery Call)
**Document Set:** 02 (Meeting Transcript)
**Pass:** Focused deep dive on use cases

---
```

---

## Mandatory Startup: Permission Check

**Every invocation, before ANY work, run this check.**

1. Read `.claude/settings.local.json`
2. Verify `Write($CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR/**)` exists in `permissions.allow`
3. Verify `WebSearch` exists in `permissions.allow`
4. If either is missing:
   - Tell the user: "Singularity requires agents to write files autonomously and research agents to search the web. I need to add `Write($CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR/**)` and/or `WebSearch` to the permissions. May I do that?"
   - If approved, add the permission
   - If declined, explain the skill cannot function and stop

---

## Invocation: "What are we doing today?"

When the user invokes `/singularity`, ask:

> **What are we doing today?**
> 1. **New engagement** - organize a new client opportunity from scratch
> 2. **Continue** - pick up where we left off on an existing engagement
> 3. **Process source** - add a new transcript, email, or document to an existing engagement
> 4. **Deliver** - draft a client-facing document
> 5. **Price** - build or refine a pricing model
> 6. **Discuss** - think through strategy or technical approach

If the user provides context that makes the intent obvious, skip this question and go directly to the right flow.

---

## Flow 1: New Engagement

**Questions to ask:**
1. What is the client name? (lowercase, underscores for folder name)
2. What is the opportunity name? (lowercase, underscores)
3. What source material do you have? (transcripts, emails, call preps, documents)
4. Do you want the full folder structure or a subset? (Default: all. Minimum: source + research.)

**Actions:**
1. Create `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/` with selected folders
2. Write `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/research/00_methodology_<date>.md` using the template at `.claude/skills/singularity/assets/templates/methodology_template.md`. Fill in the client name and opportunity description.
3. Read `.claude/context/bayone_team.md` for BayOne team context
5. Begin processing source material (proceed to Flow 3)

**Load references:** `.claude/skills/singularity/references/folder_structure.md`, `.claude/skills/singularity/references/blockchain_methodology.md`

**Full folder structure:**
```
/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/
├── org_chart.md                    (living document, always current)
├── source/                         (raw files, NEVER modified)
├── research/                       (blockchain decomposition, append-only)
├── planning/                       (skill notes, glossary, session handoffs)
├── pricing/                        (pricing specs, corrections, workbooks)
├── deliverables/                   (client-facing docs, flat with dates)
├── presentations/                  (slide decks, materials)
├── decisions/                      (open questions, agreed decisions)
└── progress/                       (status tracking)
```

---

## Flow 2: Continue Engagement

**Questions to ask:**
1. Which engagement? (client/opportunity, or detect from context)

**Actions (read in this order):**
1. `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/planning/session_handoff_<date>.md` if exists (where last session left off)
2. `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/research/00_methodology_<date>.md` (the system)
3. `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/planning/skill_notes.md` if exists (accumulated do's/don'ts)
4. Summary docs in order from `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/research/` (01 summary, 02 summary, 02a summary, etc.)
5. `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/org_chart.md` (current people state)
6. Report current state and ask what to do next

**Load references:** `.claude/skills/singularity/references/session_continuity.md`

---

## Flow 3: Process Source Material

**Questions to ask:**
1. Which engagement? (if not already established)
2. What type of source? (transcript, call prep, email, debrief, other)
3. Is this a new event (new set number) or supplementary to a prior event (letter suffix like 02a)?

**Load references:** `.claude/skills/singularity/references/document_processing.md`, `.claude/skills/singularity/references/agent_architecture.md`, `.claude/skills/singularity/references/people_tracking.md`

### Transcripts (Primary Use Case)

**Exact processing order:**

1. **Read prior context.** Latest summary in `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/research/` + `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/org_chart.md`. This ensures continuity and avoids re-discovery.
2. **Pass 1: People file.** Read the full transcript. Write the people document to `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/research/<set>_<type>_people_<date>.md`. Always the first file for transcript sets.
3. **Pass 1 continued: Topic map.** Identify major topics. Write topic map with proposed deep-dive files AND rationale for why each needs its own file. Present to user.
4. **Ask user.** Get approval on the file list. User may adjust, add, or remove files.
5. **Spawn parallel agents.** One agent per topic, ALL spawned in a single message for maximum parallelism. Each agent reads the full transcript with ONE topic focus and writes one file. See Agent Prompt Template below.
6. **Update org chart.** After all agents complete, update `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/org_chart.md` with everything learned.
7. **Bridge document.** If this is not the first set, write `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/research/<from>-<to>_changes_<date>.md`. See `.claude/skills/singularity/assets/design/gold_standards/bridge_document_example.md` for the gold standard format. Captures: hypotheses validated/invalidated/open, what we got wrong, what we got right, new information, questions answered.
8. **Summary document.** Always last. Short overview referencing all files in the set.
9. **Offer research.** If unfamiliar technologies or terms were encountered, offer to spawn research agents (see Web Research section).

### Agent Prompt Template

**Every deep-dive agent must receive this complete, self-contained prompt:**

```
You are writing a detailed decomposition document from a meeting transcript.
Read the transcript, then write one focused output file.

**Your focus:** [ONE SPECIFIC TOPIC - e.g., "Technical use cases and requirements"]

**Read this file:** /<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/source/<transcript_filename>

**Context from the topic map (so you know what to look for):**
[BULLET POINTS from the topic map for this specific topic]

**What to capture in exhaustive detail:**
- Quote or closely paraphrase key statements. Do not summarize. Decompose.
- Capture specific numbers, names, technical details, and claims.
- Note who said what when it matters for context.
- Flag open questions or unresolved points.

**IMPORTANT: Speech-to-text transcript quality.**
This transcript is speech-to-text and full of transcription errors. Use common sense:
- "concept-renade" = "confidential violation"
- "lamb GPT" = "LamGPT"
- "Spacey" = "SpaCy"
- "on pram" = "on-prem"
- "brass beam" = "Brad's team"
- "compiler" = "Copilot"
- "Gapsium" / "Kaptima" = "Capgemini"
Infer intended meaning from context. Do not take mangled words at face value.

**Write your output to:** /<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/research/<set>_<type>_<topic>_<date>.md

**Use this header format:**
# <Set Number> - <Source Type>: <Topic>

**Source:** /<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/source/<transcript_filename>
**Source Date:** <date> (<context>)
**Document Set:** <set number> (<description>)
**Pass:** Focused deep dive on <topic>

---
```

### Call Preps
Single or few passes. Propose file breakdown (situational context, discovery strategy, technical reference, people). Ask user. Write files.

### Internal Debriefs
Supplementary material using letter suffix (02a, 02b). Capture candid assessments honestly. Flag anything that must never appear in client-facing materials. Update org chart.

### Emails and Written Communications
Determine if new event or supplementary. Extract decisions, action items, new information. Usually fewer files than transcript sets.

### Working Discussions (User + Claude)
Conversation becomes a document set. Read prior context, propose discussion topics (max 5), user responds, write immediately after each exchange. Use "continued" files if discussion extends. Capture reasoning, not just conclusions. Distinguish hyperbole from commitments.

---

## Flow 4: Create Deliverable

**Questions to ask:**
1. Which engagement? (if not already established)
2. What type of deliverable?
   - Problem restatement (demonstrates understanding, no solutions)
   - Information request (prioritized asks, who can answer each)
   - Preliminary approach (initial direction, explicitly preliminary)
   - Formal proposal concise (scoped engagement with phases and pricing)
   - Formal proposal detailed (extended version with deeper technical sections)
   - Resource plan (staffing and team structure)
   - Follow-up email (markdown only, maintain momentum)
3. What is the title and cover label? (Cover labels are thematic, NOT literal. "SECURE KNOWLEDGE ENABLEMENT" not "PROBLEM RESTATEMENT".)
4. Who is the audience? (VP level? Technical? Executive?)

**Process:**
1. Draft in markdown first in `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/deliverables/<name>_<date>.md`. User reviews substance before formatting.
2. Convert to HTML using BayOne design system. Read `.claude/skills/singularity/assets/design/bayone_design_spec.md` for the complete design spec. Read the appropriate gold standard for structural reference (not fill-in-the-blanks).
3. Read `.claude/context/bayone_team.md` for cover pages and "Why BayOne" sections.
4. Offer to run `/big4` for quality review before finalizing.
5. Iterate with user until approved.
6. Output HTML to `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/deliverables/<name>_<date>.html`.

**Load references:** `.claude/skills/singularity/references/deliverables_pipeline.md`, `.claude/skills/singularity/references/anti_patterns.md`, `.claude/skills/singularity/references/professional_standards.md`

**Gold standards** (read for style and structure):

| Type | Gold Standard |
|------|--------------|
| Problem restatement | `.claude/skills/singularity/assets/design/gold_standards/problem_restatement.html` |
| Information request | `.claude/skills/singularity/assets/design/gold_standards/information_request.html` |
| Preliminary approach | `.claude/skills/singularity/assets/design/gold_standards/preliminary_approach.html` |
| Proposal (concise) | `.claude/skills/singularity/assets/design/gold_standards/poc_proposal_v5.html` |
| Proposal (detailed) | `.claude/skills/singularity/assets/design/gold_standards/poc_proposal_v5_detailed.html` |
| Bridge document | `.claude/skills/singularity/assets/design/gold_standards/bridge_document_example.md` |

---

## Flow 5: Pricing

**When to offer:** After research is complete and scope is understood. Not before.

**Process:**
1. Run structured questionnaire in batches (scope/revenue, team/costs, timeline/scenarios, margin/risk, discount strategy). See `.claude/skills/singularity/references/pricing_workflow.md` for the full questionnaire.
2. Prototype numbers in the conversation first.
3. Build pricing spec markdown in `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/pricing/pricing_spec_<date>.md`. This file doubles as a prompt for Claude in Excel.
4. **Capture the pricing discussion as a research set.** The reasoning behind pricing decisions (margin targets, team composition choices, discount strategy) goes in `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/research/<set>_discussion_pricing_strategy_<date>.md`. The pricing spec in `pricing/` is the actionable output. The research doc is the record of how and why.
5. Reference the template at `.claude/skills/singularity/assets/templates/ProjectCostingTemplate.xlsx` and the creation prompt at `.claude/skills/singularity/assets/prompts/excel_template_prompt.md`.
6. Write correction prompts as separate dated files in `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/pricing/` if iteration is needed.

**Load references:** `.claude/skills/singularity/references/pricing_workflow.md`

---

## Flow 6: Discussion

**When to proactively offer:** After 2+ document sets exist, proactively offer a strategy discussion. Say: "We have enough context to discuss BayOne's positioning for this engagement. Want to work through strategy before we draft deliverables?"

**Standard strategy questions (present as first batch):**
1. What does BayOne want from this engagement? (Staffing? Solutions? Advisory? Long-term relationship?)
2. What is our unique angle or credibility for this specific client?
3. Who has decision-making authority on the client side? Who influences but does not decide?
4. What are the explicit asks vs. implicit needs?
5. What is the competitive landscape? Who else is the client talking to?

**Process:**
1. Read prior context (latest summaries + org chart)
2. Propose discussion topics based on open threads from research
3. User responds
4. Write immediately after each exchange to `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/research/<set>_discussion_<topic>_<date>.md`. Do not accumulate.
5. Continue in batches of max 5 questions
6. Write summary when user indicates discussion is complete

**Special rules for discussions:**
- Capture the user's reasoning, not just conclusions. The "why" is as valuable as the "what."
- Flag open items explicitly. If the user says "this requires discovery" or "we need info from the sales team," that is an open item.
- Do not sanitize. Capture blunt assessments, strong opinions, and confidence claims honestly.
- Distinguish hyperbole from commitments. "I could do this in a day" is confidence in feasibility, not a timeline commitment. Do not repeat it as a planning estimate.

---

## Sibling Skills

| Skill | When to Use | How to Offer |
|-------|------------|--------------|
| `/big4` | After drafting any deliverable | "Want me to run a quality review on this before finalizing?" |
| `/pptx-extractor` | User provides .pptx source material | "This is a PowerPoint file. I can use the pptx-extractor to pull the content into markdown before processing. Want me to do that?" |
| `/pdf-extractor` | User provides .pdf source material | "This is a PDF. I can extract the content to markdown first. Want me to do that?" |
| Slide skill (TBD) | User needs presentations | Output to `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/presentations/` |

---

## Web Research

When unfamiliar technologies, companies, or terms are encountered during any phase:

1. **Flag to the user.** "I noticed references to Microsoft Purview, Azure AI Foundry, and SpaCy NER. Want me to spawn research agents to investigate these in parallel?"
2. **If approved, spawn parallel research agents.** Each agent investigates one topic using WebSearch and writes findings directly to `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/research/<set>_research_<topic>_<date>.md`.
3. **Update glossary** if one exists at `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/planning/glossary_<date>.md`.

**When to offer a glossary:** If the engagement involves 3+ unfamiliar terms, or spans a domain BayOne has not worked in before, offer to create one.

---

## Glossary (Optional)

Located at `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/planning/glossary_<date>.md`. Living document (editable, not append-only). Research agents populate it during source processing. New terms added as discovered in subsequent sets.

---

## Cross-Session Artifacts

Singularity creates markdown documents that serve as prompts for other Claude sessions:
- **Pricing specs** in `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/pricing/` become prompts for Claude in Excel
- **Correction prompts** in `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/pricing/` capture iterative feedback for Excel sessions
- **Design spec update handoffs** in `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/planning/` guide other sessions on updating shared assets

These are part of the engagement record and should have clear, dated filenames.

---

`.claude/skills/singularity/references/worked_example/` contains the complete Lam Research engagement showing every document set, bridge document, org chart, and deliverable produced by this methodology. Read through it to see what good output looks like end-to-end.

3	## Engagement Folder Structure
4	
5	When the skill is invoked for a new engagement, create the following folder structure at `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/`:
6	
7	```
8	/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/

10	│
11	├── source/                                             (raw input files. NEVER modified.)

22	│   └── ...
23	│

28	│   └── ...
29	│
30	├── pricing/                                            (pricing specs, corrections, workbooks)
31	│   ├── pricing_spec_<date>.md
32	│   ├── pricing_corrections_v<N>_<date>.md
33	│   └── ...
34	│
35	├── deliverables/                                       (client-facing documents. Dated, flat.)
36	│   ├── problem_restatement_<date>.md
37	│   ├── problem_restatement_<date>.html
38	│   ├── information_request_<date>.md
39	│   ├── information_request_<date>.html

43	│   ├── discovery_findings_<date>.html
44	│   └── ...
45	│
46	├── decisions/                                          (open questions and agreed decisions)
47	│
48	└── progress/                                           (running status tracking)
49	```
50	
51	### Folder Purposes
52	
53	| Folder | Purpose | Mutability | Dated? |
54	|--------|---------|------------|--------|
55	| `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/source/` | Raw input files (transcripts, emails, docs) | Never modified | Yes (source date) |
56	| `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/research/` | Blockchain decomposition documents | Append-only (new files, never edit old) | Yes (source date) |
57	| `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/planning/` | Approach planning, skill notes, glossary, session handoffs | Editable | Yes |
58	| `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/pricing/` | Pricing specs, correction prompts, cost models, workbooks | Editable, versioned | Yes |
59	| `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/deliverables/` | Client-facing documents (markdown + HTML) | Editable, versioned | Yes |
60	| `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/presentations/` | Slide decks, pitch materials, executive briefings | Editable, versioned | Yes |
61	| `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/decisions/` | Open questions and agreed decisions | Editable | Yes |
62	| `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/progress/` | Running status tracking | Editable | Yes |
63	
64	### Ask Before Creating
65	
66	The skill should ask the user if they want the full folder structure when starting a new engagement. Not every engagement needs every folder. The minimum is `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/source/` and `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/research/`.
67	
68	## File Naming Convention
69	
70	### Research Files
71	
72	Pattern: `<set_number>_<descriptive_name>_<source_date>.md`
73	
74	Examples (all files live in `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/research/`):
75	```
76	/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/research/00_methodology_2026-03-20.md
77	/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/research/01_call_prep_situational_context_2026-03-12.md
78	/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/research/01_call_prep_discovery_strategy_2026-03-12.md
79	/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/research/01_call_prep_people_2026-03-12.md
80	/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/research/01_call_prep_summary_2026-03-12.md
81	/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/research/01-02_changes_2026-03-12.md
82	/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/research/02_meeting_people_2026-03-12.md
83	/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/research/02_meeting_topic_map_2026-03-12.md
84	/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/research/02_meeting_technical_use_cases_2026-03-12.md
85	/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/research/02_meeting_speaker_dynamics_2026-03-12.md
86	/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/research/02_meeting_summary_2026-03-12.md
87	/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/research/02a_debrief_people_2026-03-12.md
88	/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/research/02a_debrief_internal_assessment_2026-03-12.md
89	/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/research/02a_debrief_summary_2026-03-12.md
90	/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/research/03_discussion_technical_approach_2026-03-20.md
91	/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/research/03_discussion_summary_2026-03-20.md
92	```
93	
94	### Naming Rules
95	
96	- All lowercase with underscores (snake_case)
97	- Set number prefix is always two digits (01, 02, 03... not 1, 2, 3)
98	- Supplementary sets use letter suffix (02a, 02b, 02c)
99	- Date suffix uses ISO format (YYYY-MM-DD)
100	- Date reflects the source material date, not the analysis date
101	- Descriptive name should be clear enough that someone can understand the file's purpose without opening it
102	
103	### Bridge Documents
104	
105	Pattern: `<set_from>-<set_to>_changes_<date>.md`
106	
107	Examples:
108	```
109	/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/research/01-02_changes_2026-03-12.md
110	/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/research/02-03_changes_2026-03-20.md
111	```
112	
113	Bridge documents capture what changed between two sets. They are written after both sets exist.
114	
115	### Standard File Names
116	
117	Some file names are standard across all sets:
118	
119	| File Type | Full Path | When Created |
120	|-----------|-----------|--------------|
121	| Methodology | `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/research/00_methodology_<date>.md` | Once, at engagement start |
122	| People | `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/research/<set>_<source_type>_people_<date>.md` | First file for transcript sets |
123	| Topic map | `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/research/<set>_<source_type>_topic_map_<date>.md` | After first pass of transcript |
124	| Summary | `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/research/<set>_<source_type>_summary_<date>.md` | Last file for every set |
125	| Bridge | `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/research/<from>-<to>_changes_<date>.md` | After both sets exist |
126	
127	### Deliverable Files
128	
129	Deliverables go in `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/deliverables/` as flat, dated files:
130	
131	```
132	/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/deliverables/problem_restatement_2026-03-20.md
133	/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/deliverables/problem_restatement_2026-03-20.html
134	/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/deliverables/information_request_2026-03-20.md
135	/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/deliverables/information_request_2026-03-20.html
136	/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/deliverables/preliminary_approach_2026-03-20.md
137	/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/deliverables/preliminary_approach_2026-03-20.html
138	/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/deliverables/followup_email_2026-03-20.md
139	/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/deliverables/formal_proposal_2026-04-15.md
140	/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/deliverables/formal_proposal_2026-04-15.html
141	```
142	
143	Presentations go in `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/presentations/` as flat, dated files:
144	
145	```
146	/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/presentations/discovery_findings_2026-03-20.html
147	/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/presentations/technical_approach_2026-04-01.html
148	/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/presentations/executive_briefing_2026-04-15.html
149	```
150	
151	## Document Header Format
152	
153	Every research document should start with a consistent header:
154	
155	```markdown
156	# <Set Number> - <Source Type>: <Topic>
157	
158	**Source:** `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/source/<filename>`
159	**Source Date:** <date> (<context>)
160	**Document Set:** <set number> (<description>)
161	**Pass:** <if applicable, which pass this represents>
162	
163	---
164	```
165	
166	Example:
167	```markdown
168	# 02 - Meeting: Technical Use Cases (Deep Dive)
169	
170	**Source:** `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/source/lam_meeting_3122026.txt`
171	**Source Date:** 2026-03-12 (Discovery Call)
172	**Document Set:** 02 (Meeting Transcript)
173	**Pass:** Focused deep dive on use cases
174	
175	---
176	```
177	
178	For discussion documents:
179	```markdown
180	# 03 - Discussion: Technical Approach
181	
182	**Source:** Working discussion between Colin Moore and Claude
183	**Source Date:** 2026-03-20
184	**Document Set:** 03 (Technical Approach Discussion)
185	**Context:** Post-meeting analysis, informed by Sets 01, 02, and 02a
186	
187	---
188	```

## Assistant

**Tool:** Read
```
{"file_path":"/home/cmoore/programming/ai_opportunities/.claude/skills/singularity/references/blockchain_methodology.md"}
```

---

## User

Tool Result: 1	# Blockchain Methodology
2	
3	## Core Concept
4	
5	All research documents are numbered chronologically and are append-only. Once a document is written, it is never edited or revised. New understanding, corrections, or evolving thinking gets captured in subsequent documents that reference back to earlier ones.
6	
7	This is called "blockchain style" because, like a blockchain, each entry is immutable and the chain is read forward to reconstruct the full state.
8	
9	## Why This Approach
10	
11	### 1. Chronological Progression of Thought
12	
13	Consulting engagements span multiple meetings, multiple Claude sessions, and an evolving understanding of the problem. By preserving each document as it was written, you maintain a clear record of what was known at each point in time, not a retroactively cleaned-up version.
14	
15	### 2. No Re-Explanation Tax
16	
17	A new Claude session or team member can read forward through the numbered documents and reconstruct the full arc of discovery, including where assumptions were wrong and when corrections happened. No one has to re-explain what happened or how thinking evolved.
18	
19	### 3. Order of Operations Clarity
20	
21	When information arrives from different meetings, emails, and conversations, the numbering system makes it unambiguous which information was available at which point and what informed what.
22	
23	### 4. Honest Record
24	
25	Early hypotheses that turn out to be wrong are just as valuable as correct ones. They show what was validated, what was invalidated, and why thinking evolved. This prevents revisionist history and supports better decision-making.
26	
27	## Numbering Convention
28	
29	### Document Set Number
30	
31	The prefix number (01, 02, 03...) represents a chronological document set. All files from the same source event share a prefix.
32	
33	- `01_*` = first source event processed (could be a call prep, a meeting, an email, anything)
34	- `02_*` = second source event
35	- `03_*` = third source event
36	
37	**There is nothing special about what number a set gets.** 01 is not always "call prep," 02 is not always "a meeting," 03 is not always "a discussion." The number reflects when in the project timeline the material was created or processed.
38	
39	### Descriptive Name
40	
41	The middle part of the filename describes what the file covers within that set:
42	
43	- `01_call_prep_situational_context` = situational context from the call prep
44	- `02_meeting_technical_use_cases` = technical use cases from the meeting
45	- `02a_debrief_action_items` = action items from the debrief
46	
47	### Date Suffix
48	
49	The date at the end reflects the date of the source material, not the date of analysis:
50	
51	- `01_call_prep_situational_context_2026-03-12.md` = source material is from March 12, 2026
52	
53	This makes chronological ordering unambiguous even outside the numbering system.
54	
55	### Full Example
56	
57	```
58	01_call_prep_situational_context_2026-03-12.md
59	^^                                ^^^^^^^^^^
60	|                                 Date of source material
61	Set number (first event processed)
62	```
63	
64	## Supplementary Material (Letter Suffixes)
65	
66	When supplementary material is tied to the same event as an existing document set (e.g., an internal debrief immediately after a meeting, a follow-up email the same day), use a letter suffix rather than a new number:
67	
68	- `02_meeting_*` = the meeting itself
69	- `02a_debrief_*` = internal debrief after the same meeting
70	- `02b_followup_email_*` = a follow-up email about the same meeting
71	
72	This keeps it clear that the supplementary material is event-adjacent, not a new chronological step. The same append-only rules apply.
73	
74	## Standard Files Per Set
75	
76	### Required for Every Set
77	
78	1. **Summary document** (e.g., `01_call_prep_summary_2026-03-12.md`)
79	   - Always the LAST file written for each set
80	   - Short, high-level overview of everything covered in the set
81	   - References the other files by name
82	   - Lets a new Claude session understand the set without reading every detail file
83	   - Critical because the number and type of detail files varies per set
84	
85	### Required for Sets Based on Meetings/Calls
86	
87	2. **People document** (e.g., `02_meeting_people_2026-03-12.md`)
88	   - Who was on the call, roles, titles, sentiment
89	   - Always created for any transcript-based set
90	
91	### Created at the End (After Multiple Sets Exist)
92	
93	3. **Bridge documents** (e.g., `01-02_changes_2026-03-12.md`)
94	   - Captures what changed between two document sets
95	   - What was confirmed, invalidated, or newly learned
96	   - Written retrospectively after both sets exist
97	   - Never written during processing
98	
99	### Variable Files
100	
101	Beyond the standard files, the set of detail files is not fixed. Different source events warrant different breakdowns. Common candidates:
102	
103	- Technical deep dive breakdown (by topic)
104	- Business opportunity and specific notes
105	- Meeting breakdown and speaker dynamics
106	- Action items and next steps
107	- Hypothesis validation
108	- Infrastructure analysis
109	
110	**The skill should always ask the user what files to create beyond the standard ones.** The user knows what matters. Ask, do not assume.
111	
112	## Rules
113	
114	1. Never go back and edit a numbered document after it is written.
115	2. New insights go in new documents with higher numbers.
116	3. Reference back to earlier documents by number when correcting or building on them.
117	4. Each document set covers one source event (a meeting, an email, a document, a discussion).
118	5. The methodology document (`/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/research/00_methodology_<date>.md`) is the only file that can be updated, because it describes the system itself.
119	6. The org chart (`/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/org_chart.md`) is the only other file that can be updated (see People Tracking).
120	
121	## Reading Order for a New Session
122	
123	A new Claude session picking up an engagement should read:
124	
125	1. `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/research/00_methodology_<date>.md` to understand the system
126	2. The summary documents in `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/research/` in order (01 summary, 02 summary, 02a summary, 03 summary, etc.)
127	3. `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/org_chart.md` for the current people state
128	4. `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/planning/skill_notes.md` if it exists (accumulated do's/don'ts)
129	5. `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/planning/session_handoff_<date>.md` if it exists (where the last session left off)
130	6. Then dive into specific detail files in `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/research/` as needed
131	
132	This gives full context in minutes without reading every file.
133

## User

Tool Result: 1	# Document Processing Workflow
2	
3	## Overview
4	
5	This document describes how different types of source material are processed through the skill. The workflow changes depending on the source type, but the output always follows the blockchain methodology.
6	
7	## Source Types
8	
9	### Type 1: Meeting Transcripts (Primary Use Case)
10	
11	Meeting transcripts are the most common and most complex source type. They require multi-pass reading and parallel agent execution.
12	
13	**Processing Order:**
14	
15	1. **Read prior context.** Before touching the transcript, read the previous set's summary document in `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/research/` and `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/org_chart.md`. This ensures continuity and avoids re-discovery of known information.
16	
17	2. **Pass 1: People file.** Read the full transcript once. Write the people document (who was on the call, roles, titles, sentiment for each person). This is always the first file for a transcript set.
18	
19	3. **Pass 1 continued: Topic map.** On the same or a second read, identify the major topics discussed. Write these as an outline/topic list. This becomes the roadmap for subsequent passes. Include a proposed list of detail files with rationale for why each needs its own file.
20	
21	4. **Ask the user.** Present the proposed file list. Ask if they want to adjust, add, or remove files. The user controls what gets created.
22	
23	5. **Pass 2+: Per-topic deep dives.** For each topic, read the transcript again focusing on that ONE topic. Write the documentation for that topic after that focused read. Then read again for the next topic. Write after every read, not once at the end.
24	
25	   **Agent opportunity:** In the skill, each per-topic pass should be dispatched as a separate agent running in parallel. Each agent reads the full transcript with a specific topic focus and produces one output file. This is the natural parallelization point.
26	
27	6. **Update org chart.** After all detail files are written, update `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/org_chart.md` with everything learned from the transcript.
28	
29	7. **Bridge document.** If this is not the first set, write the bridge document capturing what changed between this set and the prior one (hypotheses validated/invalidated, new information, corrections).
30	
31	8. **Summary document.** Always last. Short, high-level overview of everything in the set.
32	
33	### Type 2: Call Prep Documents
34	
35	Call prep documents are typically processed before the meeting they prepare for. They capture pre-meeting assumptions, hypotheses, strategy, and reference material.
36	
37	**Processing Order:**
38	
39	1. **Read the document.** Call preps are usually shorter and more structured than transcripts. A single read may be sufficient.
40	
41	2. **Propose file breakdown.** Based on the content, propose how to split the document. Common splits:
42	   - Situational context (who the client is, what we know)
43	   - Discovery strategy (questions to ask, signals to listen for)
44	   - Technical reference (background research, stack details)
45	   - People (known contacts and their roles)
46	
47	3. **Ask the user.** Confirm the file breakdown.
48	
49	4. **Write the files.** Can be done sequentially or in parallel depending on complexity.
50	
51	5. **Write the summary.** Last file for the set.
52	
53	### Type 3: Internal Debriefs
54	
55	Internal conversations (e.g., a sales debrief after a client meeting) are supplementary to the meeting they follow. They use the letter suffix convention (02a, 02b, etc.).
56	
57	**Processing Order:**
58	
59	1. **Read `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/org_chart.md` and the meeting summary** (in `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/research/`) that this debrief follows.
60	
61	2. **Read the debrief transcript.**
62	
63	3. **Propose file breakdown.** Common splits for internal debriefs:
64	   - People assessments (candid, internal views on client team)
65	   - Internal assessment (technical take, sales strategy, competitive intelligence)
66	   - Action items and next steps
67	
68	4. **Ask the user.** Confirm the file breakdown.
69	
70	5. **Write the files.** These are internal documents. Capture the tone honestly. Do not sanitize candid assessments, but do flag anything that should never appear in client-facing materials.
71	
72	6. **Update `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/org_chart.md`** with any new people or updated assessments.
73	
74	7. **Write the summary.** Last file for the set.
75	
76	### Type 4: Working Discussions (User + Claude)
77	
78	When the user wants to think through technical approach, strategy, or open questions with Claude, the conversation itself becomes a document set.
79	
80	**Processing Order:**
81	
82	1. **Read prior context.** Read the previous summary in `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/research/` and `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/org_chart.md`.
83	
84	2. **Claude proposes discussion topics** based on what's known, what's open, and what needs decisions. Present as a batch of questions (max 5 per batch).
85	
86	3. **User responds.**
87	
88	4. **Write immediately.** After each exchange, write the discussed topics into a research file. Do not accumulate. Do not wait until the end.
89	
90	5. **Continue the discussion.** Ask follow-up questions (max 5 per batch). Write after each exchange.
91	
92	6. **Use "continued" files** if the discussion naturally extends beyond a single document. Each file should cover a coherent chunk of discussion.
93	
94	7. **Write the summary** when the user indicates the discussion is complete.
95	
96	**Special rules for discussions:**
97	
98	- Capture the user's reasoning, not just conclusions. The "why" is as valuable as the "what."
99	- Flag open items explicitly. If the user says "this requires discovery" or "we need info from the sales team," that is an open item.
100	- Do not sanitize. Capture blunt assessments, strong opinions, and confidence claims honestly.
101	- Distinguish hyperbole from commitments. "I could do this in a day" is confidence in feasibility, not a timeline. Do not repeat it as a planning estimate.
102	
103	### Type 4a: Strategy Discussion (Proactive Offering)
104	
105	After the research library has 2+ document sets, the skill should proactively offer a strategy discussion. This is a specific variant of the working discussion focused on engagement positioning.
106	
107	**Standard Strategy Questions (present as a batch):**
108	
109	1. What does BayOne want from this engagement? (Staffing? Solutions? Advisory? Long-term relationship?)
110	2. What is BayOne's unique angle or credibility for this specific client?
111	3. Who has decision-making authority on the client side? Who influences but does not decide?
112	4. What are the client's explicit asks vs. implicit needs? (What they said they want vs. what they actually need)
113	5. What is the competitive landscape? Who else is the client talking to?
114	
115	**Output:** Captured as a standard discussion set in `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/research/`. The positioning decisions feed directly into deliverable creation.
116	
117	**When to offer:** After processing a discovery call or initial meeting transcript, when the research library has enough context to have a meaningful strategy conversation. The skill should say: "We have enough context to discuss BayOne's positioning for this engagement. Want to work through strategy before we draft deliverables?"
118	
119	### Type 5: Emails and Written Communications
120	
121	Emails, Slack messages, or other written communications can be processed as their own set or as supplementary material to a meeting.
122	
123	**Processing Order:**
124	
125	1. Determine if this is its own event (new set number) or supplementary (letter suffix).
126	2. Read the content.
127	3. Extract key information: decisions made, action items, new information, changes to prior understanding.
128	4. Write appropriate files (often fewer and shorter than transcript-based sets).
129	5. Update `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/org_chart.md` if needed.
130	6. Write summary.
131	
132	## Multi-Pass Reading: Why It Matters
133	
134	The multi-pass approach is the single most important processing rule. It exists because:
135	
136	- **Context clearing.** Each pass starts fresh with one focus. The agent reads the entire transcript but only attends to one topic. This prevents the "everything blurs together" problem.
137	- **Exhaustive capture.** Details that would be missed in a single sweep get caught because the agent is looking for one specific thing.
138	- **Better organization.** Each file is written with focused intent after a focused read, producing tighter, more purposeful documents.
139	- **Natural parallelization.** Each per-topic pass is independent, making it ideal for parallel agent execution.
140	
141	## Web Research During Source Processing
142	
143	When processing any source material, the skill should watch for unfamiliar technologies, companies, domain-specific terms, or claims that need verification. When detected:
144	
145	1. **Flag to the user.** "I noticed references to Microsoft Purview, Azure AI Foundry, and SpaCy NER. Want me to spawn research agents to investigate these in parallel?"
146	2. **Spawn parallel research agents** if the user approves. Each agent researches one topic and writes its findings to `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/research/<set>_research_<topic>_<date>.md`.
147	3. **Update the glossary** if one exists at `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/planning/glossary_<date>.md`. If the engagement involves heavy domain-specific terminology and no glossary exists yet, offer to create one.
148	4. **Incorporate findings** into subsequent research docs and deliverables.
149	
150	Research agents run in parallel with deep-dive agents when possible. For example, while 5 deep-dive agents are processing a transcript by topic, 3 research agents can simultaneously investigate unfamiliar technologies mentioned in that transcript.
151	
152	See `05_agent_architecture.md` for full research agent details (prompts, file paths, quality standards).
153	
154	## Glossary (Optional)
155	
156	Located at `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/planning/glossary_<date>.md`. Created when the engagement involves unfamiliar technology or domain-specific terminology.
157	
158	**When to create:**
159	- The skill encounters 3+ terms that need definition during source processing
160	- The user asks for one
161	- The engagement spans a domain BayOne has not worked in before
162	
163	**How it works:**
164	- Research agents populate it during source processing
165	- It is a living document (editable, not append-only)
166	- New terms are added as they are discovered in subsequent document sets
167	- Definitions include what it is, how it relates to the engagement, and source
168	
169	## Question Batching
170	
171	When asking the user follow-up questions during a discussion:
172	
173	- **Maximum 5 questions per batch.** More than 5 overwhelms the user and leads to thin answers.
174	- If you have more questions, ask them in subsequent rounds after the first batch is answered.
175	- Prioritize questions that gate decisions or unblock progress.
176	
177	## Source Material Quality
178	
179	Transcripts are almost always speech-to-text and will be full of transcription errors: misspelled names, garbled technical terms, sentence fragments, speaker misattribution. The skill (and all agents) must apply common sense when reading them.
180	
181	Examples of common transcription errors:
182	- "concept-renade" = "confidential violation"
183	- "lamb GPT" = "LamGPT"
184	- "Spacey" = "SpaCy"
185	- "on pram" = "on-prem"
186	- "kills that guy" = "builds that out"
187	- "brass beam" = "Brad's team"
188	- "compiler" = "Copilot"
189	- "Gapsium" / "Kaptima" = "Capgemini"
190	
191	Do not take mangled words at face value. Infer the intended meaning from context. The skill should instruct all spawned agents to apply this same interpretation.
192
