## User

Tool Result: 1	# Agent Architecture
2	
3	## Overview
4	
5	The skill uses spawned agents for parallelizable work, primarily the per-topic deep dives during transcript processing. Each agent reads the full transcript with a single focus and produces one output file. This is the primary performance optimization in the skill.
6	
7	## When to Use Agents
8	
9	### Use Agents For
10	
11	- **Per-topic deep dives.** After the topic map is created and approved, each topic gets its own agent. All agents run in parallel.
12	- **Research lookups.** When external information needs to be researched (e.g., Azure AI Foundry capabilities, Microsoft Purview documentation) in the context of the problem statement.
13	- **Re-exploration of existing docs.** When a specific detail needs to be found across multiple research files (e.g., "find all mentions of Azure services across all 02 files").
14	
15	### Do Not Use Agents For
16	
17	- **The people file.** This is done in the main session because it requires reading the org chart first and updating it after.
18	- **The topic map (Pass 1).** This is done in the main session because it produces the list of topics that agents will be dispatched for.
19	- **The summary document.** This synthesizes across all files in the set and must be written after all agents complete.
20	- **The bridge document.** This requires reading across two sets and is done in the main session.
21	- **The org chart update.** This requires reading the current org chart and all per-set people information.
22	- **Deliverables.** These require synthesis and user interaction.
23	
24	## Agent Prompt Template for Deep Dives
25	
26	Each agent needs a complete, self-contained prompt because agents start fresh with no context. The prompt must include:
27	
28	```
29	You are writing a detailed decomposition document from a meeting transcript.
30	Read the transcript, then write one focused output file.
31	
32	**Your focus:** [ONE specific topic]
33	
34	**Read this file:** [path to transcript]
35	
36	**Context from Pass 1 topic map (so you know what to look for):**
37	[Bullet points summarizing what the topic map identified for this topic]
38	
39	**What to capture in exhaustive detail:**
40	[Specific list of what to look for and extract]
41	
42	Be exhaustive. Quote or closely paraphrase key statements. Don't summarize - decompose.
43	
44	**IMPORTANT:** This transcript is speech-to-text and full of transcription errors.
45	Use common sense to interpret garbled words.
46	
47	**Write your output to:** [exact file path]
48	
49	Use this header format:
50	[header template]
51	```
52	
53	### Key Elements of the Agent Prompt
54	
55	1. **The transcript path.** The agent reads the full transcript itself.
56	2. **The topic focus.** Exactly one topic per agent.
57	3. **Context from the topic map.** Bullet points so the agent knows what to look for without re-discovering it.
58	4. **Exhaustive detail instructions.** "Quote or closely paraphrase. Don't summarize, decompose."
59	5. **Speech-to-text warning.** Agents must apply common-sense interpretation.
60	6. **Exact output file path.** The agent writes directly to the `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/research/` folder.
61	7. **Header template.** Consistent formatting across all files.
62	
63	## Agent Spawn Configuration
64	
65	### Permission Mode
66	
67	```javascript
68	mode: "bypassPermissions"
69	```
70	
71	This is required for agents to write files without prompting the user. It works in conjunction with the Write permission in settings (see Prerequisites).
72	
73	### Parallel Execution
74	
75	All per-topic agents should be spawned in a single message with multiple tool calls:
76	
77	```
78	// Spawn all 5 agents in ONE message
79	Agent(topic1_prompt)
80	Agent(topic2_prompt)
81	Agent(topic3_prompt)
82	Agent(topic4_prompt)
83	Agent(topic5_prompt)
84	```
85	
86	This maximizes parallelism. The agents run concurrently and return results as they complete.
87	
88	### Agent Names
89	
90	Give each agent a short, descriptive name in the `description` field:
91	
92	```
93	description: "Deep dive: technical use cases"
94	description: "Deep dive: what was tried"
95	description: "Deep dive: infrastructure and access"
96	```
97	
98	## Permission Setup
99	
100	### Required Permission
101	
102	The following must be in `.claude/settings.local.json`:
103	
104	```json
105	{
106	  "permissions": {
107	    "allow": [
108	      "Write($CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR/**)"
109	    ]
110	  }
111	}
112	```
113	
114	This grants agents write access to the entire project directory. It must be this broad because engagement folders are created at the project root (`/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/`) and client/opportunity names vary.
115	
116	With this permission and `mode: "bypassPermissions"` on agent spawns, agents write files fully autonomously with zero user approval prompts.
117	
118	### Mandatory Startup Check
119	
120	**Every time singularity is invoked, before doing ANY work, it must verify that agents can write files.** This is a hard gate. If the check fails, the skill stops and tells the user how to fix it.
121	
122	The check:
123	
124	1. Read `.claude/settings.local.json`
125	2. Verify that the `permissions.allow` array contains a Write permission that covers the project root. Acceptable patterns:
126	   - `Write($CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR/**)`  (preferred, covers everything)
127	   - `Write($CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR/<specific_client>/**)` (acceptable if the client folder is known)
128	3. If the permission is missing or too narrow:
129	   - Tell the user: "Singularity requires agents to write files autonomously. The Write permission in `.claude/settings.local.json` needs to cover the engagement folder. I need to add `Write($CLAUDE_PROJECT_DIR/**)` to the permissions. May I do that?"
130	   - If the user approves, add the permission
131	   - If the user declines, explain that the skill cannot function without it and stop
132	
133	**Why this is mandatory:** The entire skill depends on parallel agents writing research files. Without this permission, every agent write prompts the user for approval, which defeats the purpose of parallel execution and breaks the workflow. This was learned through painful trial and error.
134	
135	### How It Was Validated
136	
137	The pptx-extractor skill at `.claude/skills/pptx-extractor/` confirmed that agents can write files autonomously when the Write permission is properly configured in settings.local.json. The same pattern applies here.
138	
139	## Post-Agent Workflow
140	
141	After all agents complete:
142	
143	1. **Read all agent output files.** The main session reads every file the agents produced to understand the full picture.
144	2. **Write the synthesis files.** Summary, bridge document, org chart update. These require cross-file understanding that agents cannot provide individually.
145	3. **Inform the user.** Report what was created and the current state of the document set.
146	
147	## Error Handling
148	
149	If an agent fails to write a file:
150	- Do NOT fall back to writing the file in the main session. The user explicitly rejected this pattern.
151	- Do NOT attempt to extract agent output from temp files with scripts.
152	- Report the failure and ask the user how to proceed.
153	
154	## Research Agents
155	
156	Research agents are a distinct agent type from deep-dive agents. They perform external research using WebSearch and WebFetch, and they write their findings directly to the engagement folder. They are first-class citizens in the skill, not an afterthought.
157	
158	### What Research Agents Do
159	
160	- **Technology research:** Investigate unfamiliar technologies, frameworks, platforms, or services mentioned in meetings or source material. Example: "What is Microsoft Purview and what are its capabilities for sensitive information detection?"
161	- **Company research:** Background on client companies, competitors, market position, recent news. Example: "What does Lam Research do in the semiconductor industry?"
162	- **Benchmark research:** Industry benchmarks, market rates, competitive pricing, best practices. Example: "What do legacy UI modernization projects typically cost?"
163	- **Validation:** Verify technical claims made in meetings against current documentation. Example: "Does Azure AI Foundry support custom sensitive information types?"
164	- **Domain exploration:** Understand unfamiliar domains the client operates in. Example: "How do semiconductor fab naming conventions work?"
165	
166	### Research Agents Write Their Own Files
167	
168	Research agents write their findings directly to `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/research/` or `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/planning/` depending on the content:
169	
170	- **Technology and domain research** → `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/research/<set>_research_<topic>_<date>.md`
171	- **Glossary updates** → `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/planning/glossary_<date>.md`
172	- **Benchmark data** → `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/pricing/benchmarks_<topic>_<date>.md` (when pricing-related)
173	
174	Each research agent is spawned with `mode: "bypassPermissions"` and writes autonomously, same as deep-dive agents.
175	
176	### Parallel Research
177	
178	Multiple research agents can run in parallel when there are several independent topics to investigate. This is common when:
179	
180	- Processing a transcript that references multiple unfamiliar technologies
181	- Preparing for a discovery call and needing background on several topics
182	- Building a pricing model and needing market benchmarks across categories
183	
184	Example: After a meeting mentions Azure AI Foundry, Microsoft Purview, and SpaCy NER, three research agents can be spawned simultaneously, each investigating one technology and writing its own output file.
185	
186	### Research Agent Prompt Template
187	
188	```
189	You are a research agent for a consulting engagement. Your job is to deeply
190	investigate a specific topic and write a comprehensive research document.
191	
192	**Your research topic:** [TOPIC]
193	
194	**Context from the engagement:** [BRIEF CONTEXT about why this topic matters]
195	
196	**Research instructions:**
197	1. Use WebSearch to find current, authoritative information
198	2. Focus on: capabilities, limitations, pricing (if relevant), how it relates
199	   to the engagement context
200	3. Distinguish between facts and marketing claims
201	4. Note the date of your sources (prefer recent over old)
202	
203	**Write your findings to:** [exact file path]
204	
205	Use this header format:
206	# <Set Number> - Research: <Topic>
207	
208	**Source:** Web research
209	**Date:** <today's date>
210	**Document Set:** <set number>
211	**Context:** <why this research was needed>
212	
213	---
214	
215	[Your findings here]
216	```
217	
218	### When to Launch Research Agents
219	
220	Research agents can be launched at any point:
221	
222	- **During source processing:** When unfamiliar terms or technologies are encountered in a transcript or document
223	- **During discussion mode:** When the user raises a topic that needs external validation
224	- **During pricing:** When market benchmarks are needed
225	- **During deliverable creation:** When a claim needs verification before putting it in a client-facing document
226	- **Proactively:** The skill should offer to research when it detects unfamiliar terms. Ask the user: "I noticed several Azure services mentioned that I could research in parallel. Want me to spawn research agents for Azure AI Foundry, Microsoft Purview, and Azure AI Search?"
227	
228	### Research Output Quality
229	
230	Research agents must:
231	- Cite sources (URLs or document names)
232	- Distinguish between verified facts and claims
233	- Note when information may be outdated
234	- Flag conflicting information from different sources
235	- Write in the same professional, detailed style as deep-dive agents
236	
237	## Agent Count Considerations
238	
239	There is no fixed number of agents per set. The number depends on the topic map:
240	
241	- A simple meeting might warrant 3 agents
242	- A complex discovery call might warrant 5-7 agents
243	- An internal debrief might warrant 2-3 agents
244	
245	The topic map determines the count. The user approves the proposed file list before agents are spawned.
246	

---

## User

Tool Result: 1	# People Tracking System
2	
3	## Dual System Design
4	
5	People information is tracked in two places simultaneously. This is intentional and serves different purposes.
6	
7	### 1. Per-Set People Documents (Blockchain Style)
8	
9	Located in `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/research/`, these capture what was learned about people from a specific source event. They are append-only, like all research documents.
10	
11	**Example:** `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/research/02_meeting_people_2026-03-12.md`
12	
13	**What they capture:**
14	- Who was present (or mentioned) in that specific event
15	- Roles and titles as stated or observed
16	- Sentiment and behavioral observations from that event
17	- Relationship dynamics observed in that event
18	- New people introduced for the first time
19	- Candid assessments (for internal debriefs)
20	
21	**Why they exist:** They preserve the historical record of when information was learned. If you want to know "what did we think about Brad after the first meeting vs. after the debrief," you read the Set 02 people doc and then the Set 02a people doc.
22	
23	### 2. Living Org Chart (Always Current)
24	
25	Located at `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/org_chart.md`, this always reflects the most current and complete understanding of all people across all events.
26	
27	**What it contains:**
28	- Every person known to the engagement
29	- Their most current title, role, and relationship to the engagement
30	- A "Known Since" field indicating which set introduced them
31	- Sentiment notes that reflect the cumulative understanding
32	- A relationship map section at the bottom
33	
34	**Why it exists:** It is the quick-reference truth. A new session reads the org chart and immediately knows who everyone is, what they do, and how they relate to each other. No need to read through every per-set people doc.
35	
36	**This is the one exception to append-only.** The org chart IS updated over time because its purpose is to be a current-state reference, not a historical record.
37	
38	## Org Chart Structure
39	
40	```markdown
41	# [Engagement Name] - Org Chart
42	
43	**Last Updated:** [date] (from document set [number])
44	
45	---
46	
47	## [Client Company Name]
48	
49	### [Person Name] ("[Nickname]")
50	- **Title:** [Title]
51	- **Role in Engagement:** [Their role]
52	- **Ownership:** [What they own, if relevant]
53	- **Background:** [Career background if known]
54	- **Sentiment:** [Behavioral observations, communication style, trust signals]
55	- **Key Quote:** [One defining quote, if available]
56	- **Working Style:** [How they work, what they expect]
57	- **Known Since:** Set [number] ([source description])
58	
59	### [Next Person]
60	...
61	
62	---
63	
64	## [BayOne Solutions / Our Company]
65	
66	### [Person Name]
67	- **Title:** [Title]
68	- **Role in Engagement:** [Their role]
69	- **Relevant Experience:** [If applicable]
70	- **Meeting Performance:** [How they performed in the meeting, if applicable]
71	- **Known Since:** Set [number]
72	
73	---
74	
75	## Relationship Map
76	
77	- **[Key relationship 1]**
78	- **[Key relationship 2]**
79	- **[Competitive landscape if known]**
80	- **[Next engagement point]**
81	```
82	
83	## Workflow: Processing People Information
84	
85	### Before Processing a New Set
86	
87	1. Read `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/org_chart.md` to have full context on all known people.
88	2. Read the prior set's summary in `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/research/` for context on where we left off.
89	
90	### During Processing
91	
92	3. Create the per-set people document as the first file for transcript-based sets.
93	4. Capture everything specific to this event: who was there, what was observed, sentiment in this specific interaction.
94	
95	### After All Set Files Are Written
96	
97	5. Update `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/org_chart.md` with any new people, updated titles, new relationship information, or changed sentiment based on this set.
98	6. Update the "Last Updated" line in `/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/org_chart.md` to reflect the current set.
99	
100	## What to Capture About People
101	
102	### For Client-Side People
103	
104	| Field | What to Include |
105	|-------|----------------|
106	| Title | Official title as stated or discovered |
107	| Role in Engagement | What they do in the context of this initiative |
108	| Ownership | What they control (budget, decisions, systems, team) |
109	| Background | Career progression if known |
110	| Sentiment | Communication style, trust signals, red flags, behavioral patterns |
111	| Key Quote | One quote that captures their personality or priorities |
112	| Working Style | How they expect things to work (requirements, engagement model) |
113	| Relationship to Others | Who they defer to, who defers to them, tensions, alignments |
114	
115	### For Internal People
116	
117	| Field | What to Include |
118	|-------|----------------|
119	| Title | Official title |
120	| Role in Engagement | What they do in the context of this initiative |
121	| Relevant Experience | Why they are on this engagement |
122	| Meeting Performance | What landed well, what got redirected, strengths and weaknesses observed |
123	| Relationship to Others | Internal dynamics, who drives what |
124	
125	### For People Mentioned but Not Met
126	
127	| Field | What to Include |
128	|-------|----------------|
129	| Title | If known |
130	| Role | Expected role when they join |
131	| Context | How they were referenced and by whom |
132	| Significance | Why they matter to the engagement |
133	
134	## Handling Candid Assessments
135	
136	Internal debriefs often contain blunt, unfiltered opinions about client team members. These are valuable and should be captured honestly in the per-set people documents and reflected (more diplomatically) in the org chart.
137	
138	**Rules:**
139	- Internal debrief people docs should preserve the tone and candor of the assessment
140	- The org chart should reflect the substance of the assessment without inflammatory language
141	- Flag any assessment that could be colored by ego friction or frustration (e.g., "Colin's assessment of Mikhail may be partly influenced by being redirected on the call")
142	- Never let internal candid assessments leak into client-facing deliverables
143	
144	## Competitors and External Parties
145	
146	Competitors, prior partners, and other external parties mentioned in meetings should be tracked in the org chart's relationship map section, not as individual entries. They are contextual, not stakeholders.
147	
148	Example:
149	```markdown
150	## Relationship Map
151	
152	- **Competitive landscape:** Deloitte and Capgemini are long-term embedded incumbents.
153	  Accenture was the prior partner who attempted the text classification work and failed.
154	```
155

## User

Tool Result: 1	# Decomposition Methodology
2	
3	**Established:** <DATE>
4	**Engagement:** <CLIENT_NAME> - <OPPORTUNITY_DESCRIPTION>
5	
6	---
7	
8	## Blockchain Style Documentation
9	
10	This research folder follows a **blockchain style** approach: documents are numbered chronologically and are **append-only**. Once written, they are never edited or revised. New understanding, corrections, or evolving thinking gets captured in subsequent documents that reference back to earlier ones.
11	
12	### Why Blockchain Style
13	
14	1. **Chronological progression of thought.** This engagement will span multiple meetings, multiple Claude sessions, and an evolving understanding of the problem. By preserving each document as it was written, we maintain a clear record of what we knew at each point in time, not a retroactively cleaned-up version.
15	
16	2. **No re-explanation tax.** A new Claude session or team member can read forward through the numbered documents and reconstruct the full arc of discovery, including where assumptions were wrong and when corrections happened.
17	
18	3. **Order of operations clarity.** When information arrives from different meetings, emails, and conversations, the numbering system makes it unambiguous which information was available at which point and what informed what.
19	
20	4. **Honest record.** Early hypotheses that turn out to be wrong are just as valuable as correct ones. They show what was validated, what was invalidated, and why thinking evolved.
21	
22	### Numbering Convention
23	
24	- **Prefix number** = chronological document set (01, 02, 03...). All files from the same source event share a prefix.
25	- **Letter suffix** = supplementary material tied to the same event (02a, 02b). Used for debriefs, follow-up emails, etc.
26	- **Descriptive name** = what the file covers within that set.
27	- **Date suffix** = the date of the source material (not the date of analysis). Format: YYYY-MM-DD.
28	
29	Example: `01_call_prep_situational_context_2026-03-12.md` means this is from document set 01 (the call prep), covers situational context, and the source material is from March 12, 2026.
30	
31	### Rules
32	
33	1. Never go back and edit a numbered document after it is written.
34	2. New insights go in new documents with higher numbers.
35	3. Reference back to earlier documents by number when correcting or building on them.
36	4. Each document set covers one source event (a meeting, an email, a document, a discussion).
37	5. This methodology document is the only file in research/ that can be updated, because it describes the system itself.
38	
39	### Document Header Format
40	
41	Every research document starts with this header for traceability:
42	
43	```
44	# <Set Number> - <Source Type>: <Topic>
45	
46	**Source:** /<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/source/<filename>
47	**Source Date:** <date> (<context>)
48	**Document Set:** <set number> (<description>)
49	**Pass:** <if applicable, which pass this represents>
50	
51	---
52	```
53	
54	### Standard Files Per Set
55	
56	- **People file** (first file for transcript-based sets): Who was present, roles, titles, sentiment, dynamics.
57	- **Topic map** (after first pass): Topics identified, proposed deep-dive files with rationale.
58	- **Deep-dive files** (one per topic, agent-written in parallel): Exhaustive detail on one specific topic.
59	- **Summary file** (always last): Short, high-level overview referencing all other files in the set.
60	
61	### Bridge Documents
62	
63	Between numbered document sets, a **bridge document** captures what changed (e.g., `01-02_changes_2026-03-12.md`). These are written after both sets exist and describe:
64	- Hypotheses validated, invalidated, or still open
65	- What we got wrong or did not anticipate
66	- What we got right
67	- New information not in the prior set
68	- Questions answered from earlier open items
69	
70	Bridge documents are created at the end of processing a set, not during processing.
71	
72	### People Tracking (Dual System)
73	
74	People information is tracked in two places:
75	
76	1. **Per-set people document** (in research/, blockchain style): Captures what we learned about people from that specific source event. Append-only like everything else in research.
77	
78	2. **Living org chart** (`/<client_name>/<opportunity_name>/org_chart.md`): Always reflects the most current and complete understanding of all people across all events. This file IS updated over time. It is the one exception to append-only, because its purpose is to be a current-state reference.
79	
80	### Processing Order for New Sets
81	
82	1. Read the prior set's summary document (for context on where we left off).
83	2. Read the current org chart (for full people context).
84	3. Process the new source material (multi-pass for transcripts).
85	4. Write detail files (agents write deep dives in parallel).
86	5. Update the org chart with new information.
87	6. Write bridge document (what changed vs. prior set).
88	7. Write summary document (always last).
89	
90	### Reading Order for a New Session
91	
92	1. This methodology document.
93	2. Summary documents in order (01 summary, 02 summary, 02a summary, etc.).
94	3. The org chart.
95	4. Skill notes (if exists, in planning/).
96	5. Session handoff (if exists, in planning/).
97	6. Then dive into specific detail files as needed.
98
